                            'CYCLONE'                             2288400100029 
INC-SOURCE (P-LI7)  65 MeV proton beam strikes 3 mm thick         2288400100030 
             natural lithium target. proton current is 12 micro-A 2288400100031 
             producing aprx. 1.0E+5 neutrons/cm2/sec at the       2288400100032 
             location of the target                               2288400100033 
INC-SPECT  .Full width at half-maximum is aprx. 2 MeV containing  2288400100034 
            90% of neutrons/MeV plus a flat continuum of          2288400100035 
            low-energy neutrons.                                  2288400100036 
           -For energy calibration the proton and deuteron recoi- 2288400100037 
            ling from respectively a polypropilene (1 mm thick)   2288400100038 
            and deuterated polypropilene target (0.6 mm thick)    2288400100039 
            were used.                                            2288400100040 
           .EN-RSL-FW   Full width at the half-maximum of the     2288400100041 
                        neutron energy line                       2288400100042 
DETECTOR   (COIN,TELES,SCIN,CSICR)  Four charged particles        2288400100043 
             detector consisting of six telescopes were used      2288400100044 
             simultaneously, each of them consists of             2288400100045 
             1.  'Delta-E' Detector NE102 plastic scintillator,   2288400100046 
                  0.1 mm thick, 4 cm diameter, and                2288400100047 
             2.   Cs-I(TL) 'E' detector, crystal 22 mm thick,     2288400100048 
                  38.1 mm diameter                                2288400100049 
METHOD     (TOF)  The time-of-flight method was deduced from the  2288400100050 
              time difference between the capacitive beam pickoff 2288400100051 
              located upstream from the neutron-producing target, 2288400100052 
              and the delta-E detector. only those events of      2288400100053 
              charged particles detection  were registered which  2288400100054 
              are associated with neutrons in the main neutron    2288400100055 
              peak.                                               2288400100056 
           (COINC,EDE)                                            2288400100057 
ANALYSIS   .Interpolation and extrapolation of double-differential2288400100058 
            data were performed with the help of two-parameter    2288400100059 
            formula a*exp(b*cos(theta)), theta is angle of scatte-2288400100060 
            ring in lab. system                                   2288400100061 
MONITOR    (1-H-1(N,EL)1-H-1,,DA)   Cross sections were measured  2288400100062 
             at degrees between 20 and 70 degree with step 10 deg,2288400100063 
             110, 140 and 160 degree in each of the telescopes    2288400100064 
MONIT-REF  (,S.Benck+,J,NP/A,615,220,1997)                        2288400100065 
SAMPLE     .Natural iron target 0.5 mm thick, 6*6 cm2 surface,    2288400100066 
            Density 2.4 gram/cm2                                  2288400100067 
CORRECTION .The solid angle and thick target corrections were     2288400100068 
            made with the help of Monte Carlo simulation program  2288400100069 
ADD-RES    (THEO,COMP)  GNASH and TALYS codes were used for light 2288400100070 
              charged particles cross sections evaluation.        2288400100071 
ERR-ANALYS (MONIT-ERR)  Error of the standard H(N,P) cross section2288400100072 
           (ERR-1)  Error of the absolute scale of energy spectrum2288400100073 
           (ERR-2)  Beam monitoring error                         2288400100074 
           (ERR-3)  Solid angle correction error                  2288400100075 
           (ERR-4)  Error due to number of sample nuclei          2288400100076 
           .Error structure is taken from reference:              2288400100077 
                                     At.Data&Nucl.Data Tabl.87    2288400100078 
           >> For 62.6 MeV incident neutron energy the overall    2288400100079 
            relative uncertainties of the experimental points in  2288400100080 
            the spectra are about 5.5% for protons.  8.5% for     2288400100081 
            deuterons, 15% for tritons, 25% for alphas mainly due 2288400100082 
            to the statistics of the spectra. For all other inci- 2288400100083 
            dent neutron energies these errors are between two    2288400100084 
            and three times higher as a consequence of a lower    2288400100085 
            incident neutron flux. <<                             2288400100086 
           >>>The uncertainty of the cross section absolute scale 2288400100087 
            is about 7-8% due to uncertainties in the reference   2288400100088 
            total (N,P) cross sections (5%), beam monitoring (2%),2288400100089 
            statistics in the H(n,p) recoil proton peak (2-5%),   2288400100090 
            solid angle corrections (1%), number of target nuclei 2288400100091 
            (1%) etc. <<<                                         2288400100092
